commit 66fa84abcc08aa5e7b9f233452fd0058a34d1a92
Author: Jeff Barczewski <jeff.barczewski@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 15 11:27:28 2015 -0500

    fix async examples
    
    Some examples are broken because they call fromCallback or
    fromNodeCallback functions with too many arguments.
    
    For example:
    
    ```javascript
    var stat = Rx.Observable.fromNodeCallback(fs.stat);
    var files = ['file1.txt', 'file2.txt', 'file3.txt'];
    
    Rx.Observable
      .for(files, stat) // won't work because calls stat(x, i, obs)
    ```
    
    The `stat` fn is called with too many arguments, it is only
    expecting file, but ends up being called with (file, i, obs)
    and that causes stat to use the index `i` as the cb and not
    use the appended cb which the fromNodeCallback adds.
    
    So correct code must ensure that only the right number
    of arguments are passed so the cb will be appended to proper
    location.
    
    ```javascript
    Rx.Observable
      .for(files, function (file) { return stat(file); })
    ```
    
    Also in some cases the definition of `files` was missing so I
    added the definition for clarity.

commit f8d42967b3dc314c136b0e041c22103a7aa778e2
Author: machty <machty@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Feb 9 07:41:22 2015 -0800

    Bugfix: don’t use Ember.addListener
    
    The gets rid of unnecessary Ember-sniffing code
    that breaks any attempt to listen to events
    on raw DOM objects (unless useNativeEvents=true),
    e.g. fromEvent(window, 'resize') when Ember
    is detected.
    
    The previous block of code that handles
    jq, Angular, etc, sufficiently handles and
    Ember objects that extend Ember.Evented, so
    removing the addListener code adds no negative
    effects.
